## Chapter 8: Nonlinear Wave Interactions

### Introduction

The study of ocean waves is a complex and fascinating field, and one of the most intriguing aspects of this discipline is the nonlinear wave interactions. These interactions are fundamental to understanding the behavior of waves in the ocean, and they play a crucial role in a wide range of applications, from the design of offshore structures to the prediction of extreme weather events.

In this chapter, we will delve into the world of nonlinear wave interactions, exploring the underlying principles and theories that govern these phenomena. We will begin by introducing the basic concepts of nonlinear wave theory, including the nonlinear Schrdinger equation and the concept of wave steepness. We will then move on to discuss the various types of nonlinear wave interactions, such as wave-wave interactions, wave-current interactions, and wave-structure interactions.

We will also explore the mathematical models used to describe these interactions, including the use of Fourier series and transforms, and the application of these models to real-world problems. For example, we will discuss how these models can be used to predict the behavior of waves in the presence of nonlinear effects, such as wave steepening and wave breaking.

Finally, we will discuss some of the practical applications of nonlinear wave theory, including the design of offshore structures and the prediction of extreme weather events. We will also touch on some of the current research topics in this field, such as the role of nonlinear wave interactions in the generation of rogue waves and the impact of these interactions on the efficiency of wave energy converters.

This chapter aims to provide a comprehensive introduction to nonlinear wave interactions, suitable for both students and professionals in the field of ocean engineering. It is our hope that this chapter will serve as a valuable resource for those seeking to understand and apply the principles of nonlinear wave theory in their work.




#### 7.2b Methods for Coordinate System Translation

There are several methods for translating coordinate systems, each with its own advantages and applications. In this subsection, we will discuss two of these methods: the Gauss-Seidel method and the GeoVector method.

##### Gauss-Seidel Method

The Gauss-Seidel method is a numerical technique used for solving a system of linear equations. In the context of coordinate system translation, this method can be used to solve for the unknown coordinates of a point in a coordinate system, given the coordinates of the point in another system.

The Gauss-Seidel method is an iterative method, meaning that it requires multiple iterations to converge on a solution. The method works by solving the system of equations one variable at a time, using the values of the other variables as known quantities. This process is repeated until the values of the variables converge to a solution within a specified tolerance.

The Gauss-Seidel method can be represented mathematically as follows:

$$
\begin{align*}
x_1^{(n+1)} &= \frac{1}{a_{11}} \left( b_1 - a_{12}x_2^{(n)} - \cdots - a_{1n}x_n^{(n)} \right) \\
x_2^{(n+1)} &= \frac{1}{a_{22}} \left( b_2 - a_{21}x_1^{(n+1)} - \cdots - a_{2n}x_n^{(n)} \right) \\
&\vdots \\
x_n^{(n+1)} &= \frac{1}{a_{nn}} \left( b_n - a_{n1}x_1^{(n+1)} - \cdots - a_{nn-1}x_{n-1}^{(n+1)} \right)
\end{align*}
$$

where $x_i^{(n)}$ is the $i$-th component of the $n$-th iteration, $a_{ij}$ are the coefficients of the system, and $b_i$ are the constants.

##### GeoVector Method

The GeoVector method is a vector-based approach to coordinate system translation. This method is particularly useful when dealing with large systems of equations, as it allows for the efficient representation and manipulation of coordinate systems.

The GeoVector method represents a coordinate system as a vector, with each component of the vector representing a coordinate of a point in the system. The translation of a coordinate system from one system to another can then be represented as a vector transformation.

The GeoVector method can be represented mathematically as follows:

$$
\mathbf{x}_2 = \mathbf{A}\mathbf{x}_1
$$

where $\mathbf{x}_1$ and $\mathbf{x}_2$ are the vectors representing the coordinate systems, and $\mathbf{A}$ is the transformation matrix.

In the next section, we will discuss how these methods can be applied to the translation of coordinate systems in the context of wave dynamics.

#### 7.2c Applications of Coordinate System Translation

The translation of coordinate systems is a fundamental concept in the study of wave dynamics. It is used in a variety of applications, including the analysis of wave propagation, the design of offshore energy systems, and the study of ship dynamics. In this section, we will discuss some of these applications in more detail.

##### Wave Propagation Analysis

In the analysis of wave propagation, it is often necessary to translate coordinates from one system to another. For example, consider a wave propagating in a three-dimensional medium. The wave can be described by a system of equations in Cartesian coordinates. However, it may be more convenient to describe the wave in spherical coordinates, particularly if the wave is propagating in a direction that is not aligned with the Cartesian axes.

The translation of coordinates in this case can be represented as a transformation from Cartesian coordinates to spherical coordinates. This transformation can be represented mathematically as follows:

$$
\begin{align*}
x &= r\sin\theta\cos\phi \\
y &= r\sin\theta\sin\phi \\
z &= r\cos\theta
\end{align*}
$$

where $r$ is the radius, $\theta$ is the polar angle, and $\phi$ is the azimuthal angle.

##### Offshore Energy Systems

In the design of offshore energy systems, such as wind turbines or wave energy converters, it is often necessary to translate coordinates from a fixed reference frame to a moving frame that follows the motion of the system. This is particularly important in the design of systems that need to withstand large waves and currents.

The translation of coordinates in this case can be represented as a transformation from a fixed reference frame to a moving frame. This transformation can be represented mathematically as follows:

$$
\begin{align*}
x' &= x - v_x t \\
y' &= y - v_y t \\
z' &= z - v_z t
\end{align*}
$$

where $v_x$, $v_y$, and $v_z$ are the velocities of the moving frame in the $x$, $y$, and $z$ directions, respectively, and $t$ is time.

##### Ship Dynamics

In the study of ship dynamics, it is often necessary to translate coordinates from a fixed reference frame to a moving frame that follows the motion of the ship. This is particularly important in the analysis of ship motions under wave loads.

The translation of coordinates in this case can be represented as a transformation from a fixed reference frame to a moving frame. This transformation can be represented mathematically as follows:

$$
\begin{align*}
x' &= x - v_x t \\
y' &= y - v_y t \\
z' &= z - v_z t
\end{align*}
$$

where $v_x$, $v_y$, and $v_z$ are the velocities of the moving frame in the $x$, $y$, and $z$ directions, respectively, and $t$ is time.

In conclusion, the translation of coordinate systems is a powerful tool in the study of wave dynamics. It allows us to describe and analyze complex systems in a variety of applications.




#### 7.2c Effects of Coordinate System Translation on Wave Dynamics

The translation of coordinate systems can have significant effects on the dynamics of ocean waves. This is particularly true in the context of ship and offshore energy systems, where the translation of coordinate systems can affect the propagation and interaction of waves with these systems.

##### Effects on Wave Propagation

The translation of coordinate systems can affect the propagation of ocean waves in several ways. For instance, the translation of a coordinate system can change the direction of wave propagation, which can impact the energy transfer between different parts of the ocean. This is particularly important in the context of offshore energy systems, where the direction of wave propagation can affect the efficiency of energy extraction.

Moreover, the translation of coordinate systems can also affect the speed of wave propagation. This is because the speed of wave propagation is often dependent on the properties of the medium, such as its density and elasticity. By changing the coordinate system, we can effectively change the properties of the medium, which can in turn affect the speed of wave propagation.

##### Effects on Wave Interaction

The translation of coordinate systems can also affect the interaction of waves with ship and offshore energy systems. For instance, the translation of a coordinate system can change the location of a ship or an offshore energy system relative to a wave, which can affect the way the wave interacts with the system. This can be particularly important in the context of wave energy extraction, where the interaction of waves with offshore energy systems is a key factor.

Furthermore, the translation of coordinate systems can also affect the forces exerted by waves on ships and offshore energy systems. This is because the forces exerted by waves are often dependent on the properties of the waves, such as their amplitude and direction. By changing the coordinate system, we can effectively change the properties of the waves, which can in turn affect the forces exerted by the waves.

In conclusion, the translation of coordinate systems can have significant effects on the dynamics of ocean waves. These effects can be particularly important in the context of ship and offshore energy systems, where the translation of coordinate systems can affect the propagation and interaction of waves with these systems.




#### 7.3a Wave Equations in Moving Coordinate Systems

In the previous section, we discussed the effects of coordinate system translation on wave dynamics. Now, we will delve into the mathematical representation of wave equations in moving coordinate systems.

##### LinardWiechert Potential

The LinardWiechert potential is a solution to the nonhomogeneous electromagnetic wave equation. It is defined as:

$$
\varphi(\mathbf{r}, t) = \frac{\delta(t' - t_r)}{1 - \boldsymbol{\beta}_s \cdot (\mathbf{r}-\mathbf{r}_s)/|\mathbf{r}-\mathbf{r}_s|}
$$

where $\boldsymbol{\beta}_s = \mathbf{v}_s/c$ and $\mathbf{r}_s$ are evaluated at the retarded time $t_r$, and we have used the identity $|\mathbf{x}|' = \hat{\mathbf{x}} \cdot \mathbf{v}$ with $\mathbf{v} = \mathbf{x}'$. The retarded time $t_r$ is the solution of the equation $t_r = t - \frac{1}{c} |\mathbf{r} - \mathbf{r}_s(t_r)|$. The delta function picks out $t' = t_r$, and

$$
\mathbf{A}(\mathbf{r}, t) = \frac{\delta(t' - t_r)}{1 - \boldsymbol{\beta}_s \cdot (\mathbf{r}-\mathbf{r}_s)/|\mathbf{r}-\mathbf{r}_s|}
$$

##### Lorenz Gauge, Electric and Magnetic Fields

In order to calculate the derivatives of $\varphi$ and $\mathbf{A}$, it is convenient to first compute the derivatives of the retarded time. Taking the derivatives of both sides of its defining equation (remembering that $\mathbf{r_s} = \mathbf{r_s}(t_r)$):

$$
\frac{d t_r}{d t} + \frac{1}{c}\frac{d t_r}{d t}\frac{d |\mathbf{r}-\mathbf{r_s}|}{d t_r}= 1
$$

Differentiating with respect to $t$,

$$
\frac{d^2 t_r}{d t^2} + \frac{1}{c}\frac{d^2 t_r}{d t^2}\frac{d |\mathbf{r}-\mathbf{r_s}|}{d t_r}= 0
$$

Differentiating again with respect to $t$,

$$
\frac{d^3 t_r}{d t^3} + \frac{1}{c}\frac{d^3 t_r}{d t^3}\frac{d |\mathbf{r}-\mathbf{r_s}|}{d t_r}= 0
$$

These derivatives can be used to calculate the derivatives of $\varphi$ and $\mathbf{A}$, and hence the electric and magnetic fields. This is a crucial step in understanding the interaction of waves with moving coordinate systems, and will be further explored in the next section.

#### 7.3b Wave Equations in Translating Systems

In the previous section, we discussed the wave equations in moving coordinate systems. Now, we will extend our discussion to translating systems, where the coordinate system is not only moving but also changing in time.

##### Translating Coordinate Systems

A translating coordinate system is a coordinate system that is moving and changing in time. This can be represented mathematically as:

$$
\mathbf{r}(t) = \mathbf{r}_0 + \mathbf{v}t
$$

where $\mathbf{r}_0$ is the initial position of the coordinate system and $\mathbf{v}$ is the constant velocity of the coordinate system.

##### Wave Equations in Translating Systems

The wave equations in translating systems can be derived from the wave equations in moving coordinate systems. The key difference is that the retarded time $t_r$ is now a function of time, and the velocity $\mathbf{v}$ is no longer constant.

The wave equations in translating systems can be written as:

$$
\frac{\partial^2 \varphi}{\partial t^2} - c^2 \nabla^2 \varphi = 0
$$

$$
\frac{\partial^2 \mathbf{A}}{\partial t^2} - c^2 \nabla^2 \mathbf{A} = 0
$$

where $\nabla^2$ is the Laplacian operator. These equations describe the propagation of electromagnetic waves in a translating coordinate system.

##### Lorenz Gauge in Translating Systems

The Lorenz gauge is a crucial concept in the study of wave equations in translating systems. It is defined as:

$$
\nabla \cdot \mathbf{A} + \frac{1}{c}\frac{\partial \varphi}{\partial t} = 0
$$

In translating systems, the Lorenz gauge takes the form:

$$
\nabla \cdot \mathbf{A} + \frac{1}{c}\frac{\partial \varphi}{\partial t} = \frac{1}{c}\frac{\partial}{\partial t}\left(\frac{\delta(t' - t_r)}{1 - \boldsymbol{\beta}_s \cdot (\mathbf{r}-\mathbf{r}_s)/|\mathbf{r}-\mathbf{r}_s|}\right) = 0
$$

This equation is crucial in the calculation of the electric and magnetic fields in translating systems. It allows us to express the electric and magnetic fields in terms of the scalar and vector potentials, and their derivatives.

In the next section, we will discuss the solutions to these wave equations in translating systems, and their physical interpretation.

#### 7.3c Applications in Wave Propagation

The wave equations in translating systems, as we have seen, describe the propagation of electromagnetic waves in a translating coordinate system. This is particularly relevant in the study of ocean wave interaction with ships and offshore energy systems.

##### Wave Propagation in Translating Systems

The LinardWiechert potential is defined as:

$$
\mathbf{A}(\mathbf{r}, t) = \frac{\delta(t' - t_r)}{1 - \boldsymbol{\beta}_s \cdot (\mathbf{r}-\mathbf{r}_s)/|\mathbf{r}-\mathbf{r}_s|}

##### Wave Propagation in Translating Systems

## Chapter 8: Wave Interactions with Ships

### Introduction

The interaction of ocean waves with ships is a complex and critical aspect of marine engineering and naval architecture. This chapter, "Wave Interactions with Ships," delves into the intricate dynamics of these interactions, providing a comprehensive guide to understanding and predicting how waves interact with ships.

The study of wave interactions with ships is not just about understanding the physical phenomena. It is also about predicting the behavior of ships in various sea conditions, designing ships that can withstand these interactions, and ensuring the safety and comfort of those on board. 

In this chapter, we will explore the fundamental principles that govern wave interactions with ships, including the effects of wave height, frequency, and direction. We will also discuss the various types of ships and how they respond differently to waves. 

We will delve into the mathematical models that describe these interactions, using the powerful language of differential equations and linear systems. For example, we might represent the motion of a ship in a wave field as a system of differential equations:

$$
\frac{d^2 x}{dt^2} = g - \frac{1}{m} \frac{d}{dt} \left( \rho \frac{dx}{dt} \right)
$$

where $x$ is the displacement of the ship, $t$ is time, $g$ is the acceleration due to gravity, $m$ is the mass of the ship, $\rho$ is the density of the water, and $v$ is the velocity of the ship.

By the end of this chapter, you should have a solid understanding of the principles and mathematics of wave interactions with ships, and be able to apply this knowledge to practical problems in marine engineering and naval architecture.

The depth of the ocean plays a significant role in how waves behave, and it is crucial to consider when designing offshore structures. We will also discuss the effects of ocean currents on wave propagation and how they can be modeled using the advection-diffusion equation.

Finally, we will examine the interaction of waves with offshore structures, such as oil rigs and wave energy converters. This is a critical aspect of understanding the behavior of waves and designing effective offshore structures. We will also discuss the effects of wave propagation on ship dynamics and how it can be modeled using the wave-ship interaction equation.

## Chapter: Ocean Wave Interaction with Ships and Offshore Energy Systems: A Comprehensive Guide

### Introduction

In this chapter, we will explore the topic of wave propagation in the ocean. This is a crucial aspect of understanding the behavior of waves and their interaction with ships and offshore energy systems. Wave propagation refers to the movement of waves through the ocean, and it is influenced by various factors such as water depth, ocean currents, and the presence of obstacles. Understanding wave propagation is essential for predicting the behavior of waves and designing effective offshore structures.

We will begin by discussing the basics of wave propagation, including the different types of waves and their properties. We will then delve into the mathematical models used to describe wave propagation, such as the wave equation and the Navier-Stokes equations. These models will help us understand the behavior of waves in different ocean conditions and their interaction with ships and offshore structures.

Next, we will explore the effects of water depth on wave propagation. The depth of the ocean plays a significant role in how waves behave, and it is crucial to consider when designing offshore structures. We will also discuss the effects of ocean currents on wave propagation and how they can be modeled using the advection-diffusion equation.

Finally, we will examine the interaction of waves with offshore structures, such as oil rigs and wave energy converters. This is a critical aspect of understanding the behavior of waves and designing effective offshore structures. We will also discuss the effects of wave propagation on ship dynamics and how it can be modeled using the wave-ship interaction equation.

## Chapter 8: Wave Propagation:




### Introduction

The study of ocean waves and their interaction with ships and offshore energy systems is a complex and multifaceted field. It is a field that has been studied extensively for decades, yet there are still many unanswered questions and areas of research to be explored. In this chapter, we will delve into the topic of ship Kelvin wakes, a phenomenon that has been of particular interest to researchers in recent years.

The Kelvin wake is a type of wave that is generated by a moving ship. It is a longitudinal wave that propagates along the length of the ship, and it is named after the British physicist Lord Kelvin who first described it in the late 19th century. The Kelvin wake is a significant component of the overall wave field generated by a ship, and it plays a crucial role in the interaction between ships and waves.

In this chapter, we will explore the fundamental principles that govern the generation and propagation of Kelvin wakes. We will discuss the mathematical models that describe these waves, and we will examine the various factors that influence their formation and evolution. We will also look at the practical implications of Kelvin wakes for ship design and operation, as well as for offshore energy systems.

The study of ship Kelvin wakes is not only of academic interest, but it also has important practical implications. Understanding these waves can help us design more efficient ships, reduce wave-induced vibrations, and improve the safety and reliability of offshore energy systems. By the end of this chapter, readers will have a comprehensive understanding of ship Kelvin wakes and their role in ocean wave interaction.




### Section: 8.1 Kelvin Wake Formation:

The Kelvin wake is a phenomenon that is observed when a ship or other object moves through water. It is a longitudinal wave that propagates along the length of the object, and it is named after the British physicist Lord Kelvin who first described it in the late 19th century. The Kelvin wake is a significant component of the overall wave field generated by a ship, and it plays a crucial role in the interaction between ships and waves.

#### 8.1a Definition of Kelvin Wake

The Kelvin wake is a type of wave that is generated by a moving ship. It is a longitudinal wave that propagates along the length of the ship, and it is named after the British physicist Lord Kelvin who first described it in the late 19th century. The Kelvin wake is a significant component of the overall wave field generated by a ship, and it plays a crucial role in the interaction between ships and waves.

The Kelvin wake is characterized by two wake lines that form the arms of a chevron, V, with the source of the wake at the vertex of the V. For sufficiently slow motion, each wake line is offset from the path of the wake source by around arcsin(1/3) = 19.47 and is made up of feathery wavelets angled at roughly 53 to the path.

The inside of the V (of total opening 39 as indicated above) is filled with transverse curved waves, each of which resembles an arc of a circle centered at a point lying on the path at a distance twice that of the arc to the wake source. This part of the pattern is independent of the speed and size of the wake source over a significant range of values.

However, at higher speeds (specifically, at large Froude number) other parts of the pattern come into play. At the tips of the transverse wave arcs their crests turn around and continue inside the V cone and towards the source, forming an overlapping pattern of narrower waves directed outside of the cone. As the source's speed increases, these shorter waves begin to dominate and form a second V within the pattern, which grows narrower as the increased speed of the source emphasizes the shorter waves that are closer to the source's path.

The angles in this pattern are not intrinsic properties of merely water: Any isentropic and incompressible liquid with low viscosity will exhibit the same phenomenon. Furthermore, this phenomenon has nothing to do with turbulence. Everything discussed here is based on the linear theory of an ideal fluid, cf. Airy wave theory.

Parts of the pattern may be obscured by the effects of propeller wash, and tail eddies behind the boat's stern, and by the boat being a large object and not a point source. The water need not be stationary, but may be moving with a steady velocity. The Kelvin wake pattern is a result of the interaction between the ship and the water, and it is a complex phenomenon that is still being studied and understood.

#### 8.1b Formation of Kelvin Wake

The formation of the Kelvin wake is a result of the interaction between the ship and the water. As the ship moves through the water, it creates a disturbance that propagates away from the ship in the form of a wave. This wave is a longitudinal wave, meaning that it propagates along the length of the ship. The wave is characterized by two wake lines that form the arms of a chevron, V, with the source of the wake at the vertex of the V.

For sufficiently slow motion, each wake line is offset from the path of the wake source by around arcsin(1/3) = 19.47 and is made up of feathery wavelets angled at roughly 53 to the path. This offset and angle are not intrinsic properties of the water, but rather a result of the specific characteristics of the ship and its motion.

The inside of the V (of total opening 39 as indicated above) is filled with transverse curved waves, each of which resembles an arc of a circle centered at a point lying on the path at a distance twice that of the arc to the wake source. This part of the pattern is independent of the speed and size of the wake source over a significant range of values.

However, at higher speeds (specifically, at large Froude number) other parts of the pattern come into play. At the tips of the transverse wave arcs their crests turn around and continue inside the V cone and towards the source, forming an overlapping pattern of narrower waves directed outside of the cone. As the source's speed increases, these shorter waves begin to dominate and form a second V within the pattern, which grows narrower as the increased speed of the source emphasizes the shorter waves that are closer to the source's path.

The formation of the Kelvin wake is a complex phenomenon that is still being studied and understood. It is influenced by a variety of factors, including the speed and size of the wake source, the properties of the water, and the specific characteristics of the ship. Understanding the formation of the Kelvin wake is crucial for predicting and mitigating the effects of ship wakes on marine ecosystems and offshore energy systems.

#### 8.1c Applications of Kelvin Wake

The Kelvin wake, as we have seen, is a complex and fascinating phenomenon that is still being studied and understood. Its applications, however, are numerous and far-reaching. In this section, we will explore some of the key applications of the Kelvin wake in various fields.

##### Marine Navigation

The Kelvin wake is a crucial factor in marine navigation, particularly for large ships. The wake lines of the Kelvin wake can be used as a reference point for determining the direction and speed of a ship. This is particularly useful in low visibility conditions, such as fog or heavy rain, where other navigation methods may be less reliable.

##### Oceanography

In the field of oceanography, the Kelvin wake is used to study ocean currents and wave propagation. The Kelvin wake is a self-propagating wave, meaning that it can travel long distances without losing energy. This makes it an ideal tool for studying ocean currents, as it can provide valuable information about the direction and speed of water movement.

##### Offshore Energy Systems

The Kelvin wake plays a crucial role in the design and operation of offshore energy systems, such as wind turbines and wave energy converters. The Kelvin wake can significantly affect the performance of these systems, and understanding its formation and characteristics is essential for optimizing their design.

##### Environmental Impact Assessment

The Kelvin wake is also a key factor in environmental impact assessments. The wake lines of the Kelvin wake can be used to assess the impact of ship traffic on marine ecosystems. This is particularly important in areas where marine life is sensitive to disturbance, such as around offshore energy systems or in protected areas.

##### Ship Design

In ship design, the Kelvin wake is used to optimize the performance of ships. By understanding the formation of the Kelvin wake, engineers can design ships that minimize the generation of wake lines, reducing their impact on marine ecosystems and offshore energy systems.

In conclusion, the Kelvin wake is a complex and fascinating phenomenon with numerous applications. Its study is crucial for a wide range of fields, from marine navigation to environmental impact assessment. As our understanding of the Kelvin wake continues to grow, so too will its potential applications.




### Section: 8.1b Mechanisms of Kelvin Wake Formation

The formation of the Kelvin wake is a complex process that involves the interaction of various forces and factors. These include the shape and size of the ship, the speed and direction of the ship, the properties of the water, and the effects of rotation and stratification.

#### 8.1b.1 Ship Shape and Size

The shape and size of the ship play a significant role in the formation of the Kelvin wake. The length and width of the ship, as well as its draft, determine the size and shape of the wake. Longer and wider ships tend to generate larger and more complex wakes, while deeper drafts can lead to deeper and more pronounced wakes.

#### 8.1b.2 Ship Speed and Direction

The speed and direction of the ship also have a profound impact on the formation of the Kelvin wake. The speed of the ship determines the frequency and amplitude of the waves, with faster ships generating higher frequencies and larger amplitudes. The direction of the ship, on the other hand, determines the orientation of the wake. If the ship is moving in a straight line, the wake will form a V-shape with the source at the vertex. If the ship is turning, the wake will take on a more complex shape, with the V-shape becoming distorted.

#### 8.1b.3 Water Properties

The properties of the water, such as its density and viscosity, also play a role in the formation of the Kelvin wake. Density differences between the water and the ship can lead to buoyancy effects, which can alter the shape and size of the wake. Viscosity, on the other hand, affects the dissipation of the wake, with higher viscosities leading to more rapid dissipation.

#### 8.1b.4 Rotation and Stratification

Rotation and stratification can also have a significant impact on the formation of the Kelvin wake. Rotation can lead to the formation of eddies and vortices, which can alter the shape and size of the wake. Stratification, on the other hand, can lead to the formation of layers of water with different densities, which can affect the propagation of the waves.

In conclusion, the formation of the Kelvin wake is a complex process that involves the interaction of various forces and factors. Understanding these mechanisms is crucial for predicting and mitigating the effects of ship wakes on marine ecosystems and offshore energy systems.

### Conclusion

In this chapter, we have delved into the complex and fascinating world of ship Kelvin wakes. We have explored the fundamental principles that govern their formation and propagation, and have examined the various factors that can influence their behavior. We have also discussed the practical implications of these phenomena, particularly in the context of offshore energy systems.

The Kelvin wake is a critical component of the overall wave field generated by a ship. Its formation is governed by a complex interplay of factors, including the ship's speed, the properties of the water, and the presence of any obstacles. The propagation of the Kelvin wake is also influenced by these factors, as well as by the rotation of the Earth and the stratification of the water.

Understanding the Kelvin wake is crucial for a variety of applications, including the design and operation of offshore energy systems. These systems are often located in regions where the wave field is dominated by the Kelvin wake, and understanding its behavior can help to optimize their performance and reliability.

In conclusion, the study of the Kelvin wake is a rich and rewarding field, offering many opportunities for further research and application. As our understanding of these phenomena continues to grow, so too will our ability to harness their potential for the benefit of society.

## Chapter 9: Ship Motions and Responses to Waves:



### Section: 8.2 Kelvin Wake Characteristics:

The Kelvin wake is a complex phenomenon that is influenced by various factors, including ship speed, water depth, and wave conditions. In this section, we will explore the characteristics of the Kelvin wake and how they are affected by these factors.

#### 8.2a Characteristics of Kelvin Wake

The Kelvin wake is characterized by its V-shaped pattern, which is formed by two wake lines that are offset from the path of the wake source. This pattern is a result of the interference between the waves generated by the ship and the waves already present in the water. The offset of the wake lines is approximately 19.47, which is determined by the arcsin(1/3) formula.

The inside of the V is filled with transverse curved waves, each of which resembles an arc of a circle. These waves are centered at a point lying on the path of the wake source, at a distance twice that of the arc to the source. This part of the pattern is independent of the speed and size of the wake source over a significant range of values.

However, at higher speeds, other parts of the pattern come into play. At the tips of the transverse wave arcs, their crests turn around and continue inside the V cone and towards the source. This results in an overlapping pattern of narrower waves directed outside of the cone. As the source's speed increases, these shorter waves begin to dominate and form a second V within the pattern, which grows narrower as the increased speed of the source emphasizes the shorter waves that are closer to the source's path.

The angles in this pattern are not intrinsic properties of merely water. Any isentropic and incompressible liquid with low viscosity will exhibit the same phenomenon. Furthermore, this phenomenon has nothing to do with turbulence. Everything discussed here is based on the linear theory of an ideal fluid, cf. Airy wave theory.

Parts of the pattern may be obscured by the effects of propeller wash, and tail eddies behind the boat's stern, and by the boat being a large object and not a point source. The water need not be stationary, but may be moving at a constant velocity. The Kelvin wake is a dynamic phenomenon that is constantly changing as the ship moves through the water.

In the next section, we will explore the effects of the Kelvin wake on ships and offshore energy systems.





### Subsection: 8.2b Measurement of Kelvin Wake Characteristics

The measurement of Kelvin wake characteristics is a crucial aspect of understanding and predicting the behavior of ships and offshore energy systems in the ocean. This subsection will discuss the various methods and techniques used to measure the characteristics of the Kelvin wake.

#### 8.2b.1 Direct Measurement

Direct measurement of the Kelvin wake characteristics involves the use of sensors and instruments to collect data on the wake patterns. This can be done using a variety of sensors, including accelerometers, gyroscopes, and wave sensors. These sensors can be mounted on the ship or offshore energy system to collect data on the wake patterns.

#### 8.2b.2 Indirect Measurement

Indirect measurement of the Kelvin wake characteristics involves the use of mathematical models and simulations to predict the wake patterns. These models and simulations take into account factors such as ship speed, water depth, and wave conditions to predict the characteristics of the Kelvin wake.

#### 8.2b.3 Remote Sensing

Remote sensing techniques, such as radar and satellite imaging, can also be used to measure the characteristics of the Kelvin wake. These techniques allow for the collection of data from a distance, making it possible to monitor the wake patterns of multiple ships and offshore energy systems simultaneously.

#### 8.2b.4 Laboratory Experiments

Laboratory experiments can be conducted to study the characteristics of the Kelvin wake in controlled environments. These experiments involve the use of wave tanks and scale models to simulate real-world conditions and collect data on the wake patterns.

In conclusion, the measurement of Kelvin wake characteristics is a complex and multifaceted process that involves a combination of direct and indirect methods. By understanding and predicting the characteristics of the Kelvin wake, we can improve the safety and efficiency of ships and offshore energy systems in the ocean.




### Subsection: 8.2c Effects of Kelvin Wake on Ship Dynamics

The Kelvin wake, as discussed in the previous sections, is a complex phenomenon that affects the dynamics of ships and offshore energy systems. In this subsection, we will delve deeper into the effects of the Kelvin wake on ship dynamics.

#### 8.2c.1 Ship Maneuverability

The Kelvin wake can significantly impact the maneuverability of a ship. The formation of the Kelvin wake behind a ship can create a region of turbulent water, which can increase the drag force acting on the ship. This increased drag can make it more difficult for the ship to change direction or speed, particularly in the presence of strong currents or waves.

#### 8.2c.2 Ship Stability

The Kelvin wake can also affect the stability of a ship. The formation of the Kelvin wake can cause a change in the hydrodynamic forces acting on the ship, which can lead to a change in the ship's center of buoyancy. This change can cause the ship to heel or roll, particularly in the presence of strong waves or currents.

#### 8.2c.3 Ship Noise and Vibration

The Kelvin wake can also contribute to the noise and vibration levels on a ship. The turbulent water behind the ship can create noise and vibrations that can be transmitted into the ship's structure. This can lead to increased levels of noise and vibration on the ship, which can be a source of discomfort for crew members and can also affect the performance of sensitive equipment.

#### 8.2c.4 Ship Performance

The Kelvin wake can also affect the overall performance of a ship. The increased drag and changes in hydrodynamic forces can lead to a decrease in the ship's speed and efficiency. This can be particularly problematic for ships operating in high-speed or high-wave conditions, where the effects of the Kelvin wake can be more pronounced.

In conclusion, the Kelvin wake plays a crucial role in the dynamics of ships and offshore energy systems. Understanding the characteristics and effects of the Kelvin wake is essential for the design, operation, and safety of these systems.

### Conclusion

In this chapter, we have delved into the complex and fascinating world of ship Kelvin wakes. We have explored the fundamental principles that govern their formation and evolution, and have examined the various factors that can influence their characteristics. We have also discussed the practical implications of ship Kelvin wakes, particularly in the context of offshore energy systems.

The Kelvin wake is a critical aspect of ship dynamics, and understanding its behavior is crucial for the design and operation of ships and offshore energy systems. The Kelvin wake can significantly impact the performance and efficiency of these systems, and can even pose safety risks if not properly managed. By studying the Kelvin wake, we can gain valuable insights into the behavior of waves and their interaction with ships, which can inform the design of more efficient and resilient systems.

In conclusion, the study of ship Kelvin wakes is a rich and rewarding field, with many opportunities for further research and application. As we continue to develop and refine our understanding of the Kelvin wake, we can look forward to significant advancements in the design and operation of ships and offshore energy systems.

The Kelvin wake is a critical aspect of ship dynamics, and understanding its behavior is crucial for the design and operation of ships and offshore energy systems. The Kelvin wake can significantly impact the performance and efficiency of these systems, and can even pose safety risks if not properly managed. By studying the Kelvin wake, we can gain valuable insights into the behavior of waves and their interaction with ships, which can inform the design of more efficient and resilient systems.

In conclusion, the study of ship Kelvin wakes is a rich and rewarding field, with many opportunities for further research and application. As we continue to develop and refine our understanding of the Kelvin wake, we can look forward to significant advancements in the design and operation of ships and offshore energy systems.

## Chapter: Chapter 9: Wave-Structure Interaction

### Introduction

The interaction between waves and structures is a complex and fascinating field of study. This chapter, "Wave-Structure Interaction," delves into the intricate dynamics of this interaction, focusing on the ocean waves and their interaction with ships and offshore energy systems. 

The ocean is a vast and dynamic environment, and the waves that move across its surface are a significant force to be reckoned with. They can exert immense pressure on structures, causing vibrations and potentially leading to structural failure if not properly accounted for in the design process. Understanding the principles of wave-structure interaction is therefore crucial for the design and operation of ships and offshore energy systems.

In this chapter, we will explore the fundamental principles that govern wave-structure interaction, including the concepts of wave propagation, reflection, and refraction. We will also delve into the mathematical models that describe these phenomena, using the powerful language of differential equations and linear algebra. For instance, the wave-structure interaction can be described by the equation `$\Delta w = \frac{\partial^2 w}{\partial t^2} - c^2 \frac{\partial^2 w}{\partial x^2}$`, where `$\Delta w$` is the wave displacement, `$t$` is time, `$x$` is the spatial coordinate, and `$c$` is the wave speed.

We will also discuss the practical implications of wave-structure interaction, including its impact on the design and operation of ships and offshore energy systems. This includes the design of structures to withstand wave forces, the prediction of wave-induced vibrations, and the optimization of energy efficiency in offshore systems.

By the end of this chapter, you should have a solid understanding of the principles of wave-structure interaction and be able to apply this knowledge to the design and operation of ships and offshore energy systems. Whether you are a student, a researcher, or a professional in the field, this chapter will provide you with the tools and knowledge you need to navigate the complex world of wave-structure interaction.




#### 8.3a Effects of Kelvin Wake on Ship Motion

The Kelvin wake, as we have seen, is a complex phenomenon that affects the dynamics of ships and offshore energy systems. In this section, we will delve deeper into the effects of the Kelvin wake on ship motion.

#### 8.3a.1 Ship Motion in Kelvin Wake

The Kelvin wake can significantly affect the motion of a ship. The formation of the Kelvin wake behind a ship can create a region of turbulent water, which can increase the drag force acting on the ship. This increased drag can make it more difficult for the ship to change direction or speed, particularly in the presence of strong currents or waves.

The Kelvin wake can also affect the stability of a ship. The formation of the Kelvin wake can cause a change in the hydrodynamic forces acting on the ship, which can lead to a change in the ship's center of buoyancy. This change can cause the ship to heel or roll, particularly in the presence of strong waves or currents.

#### 8.3a.2 Ship Noise and Vibration in Kelvin Wake

The Kelvin wake can also contribute to the noise and vibration levels on a ship. The turbulent water behind the ship can create noise and vibrations that can be transmitted into the ship's structure. This can lead to increased levels of noise and vibration on the ship, which can be a source of discomfort for crew members and can also affect the performance of sensitive equipment.

#### 8.3a.3 Ship Performance in Kelvin Wake

The Kelvin wake can also affect the overall performance of a ship. The increased drag and changes in hydrodynamic forces can lead to a decrease in the ship's speed and efficiency. This can be particularly problematic for ships operating in high-speed or high-wave conditions, where the effects of the Kelvin wake can be more pronounced.

In the next section, we will explore the methods and techniques used to study and model the Kelvin wake, and how these can be used to predict and mitigate its effects on ship motion.

#### 8.3b Mitigation of Kelvin Wake Effects

The effects of the Kelvin wake on ship motion can be mitigated through various strategies. These strategies aim to reduce the formation of the Kelvin wake, thereby reducing the increased drag and changes in hydrodynamic forces. 

#### 8.3b.1 Ship Design and Configuration

One of the most effective ways to mitigate the effects of the Kelvin wake is through ship design and configuration. The shape and size of the ship can significantly influence the formation of the Kelvin wake. For instance, a ship with a streamlined hull can reduce the formation of the Kelvin wake, thereby reducing the increased drag and changes in hydrodynamic forces. 

Moreover, the placement of the propellers and other appendages can also play a crucial role. By strategically placing the propellers and other appendages, the formation of the Kelvin wake can be minimized, thereby reducing the effects on ship motion.

#### 8.3b.2 Propulsion Systems

The propulsion system of a ship can also play a significant role in mitigating the effects of the Kelvin wake. By optimizing the propulsion system, the formation of the Kelvin wake can be minimized, thereby reducing the increased drag and changes in hydrodynamic forces.

For instance, the use of water jets or azimuth thrusters can be effective in mitigating the effects of the Kelvin wake. These propulsion systems can provide additional control and thrust, thereby reducing the effects of the Kelvin wake on ship motion.

#### 8.3b.3 Ship Operation and Maintenance

The operation and maintenance of a ship can also play a crucial role in mitigating the effects of the Kelvin wake. Regular maintenance of the ship can help in identifying and addressing any issues that can contribute to the formation of the Kelvin wake.

Moreover, the operation of the ship can also be optimized to minimize the effects of the Kelvin wake. For instance, the speed of the ship can be adjusted to minimize the formation of the Kelvin wake, thereby reducing the effects on ship motion.

In conclusion, the effects of the Kelvin wake on ship motion can be mitigated through various strategies. These strategies aim to reduce the formation of the Kelvin wake, thereby reducing the increased drag and changes in hydrodynamic forces. By implementing these strategies, the performance and efficiency of a ship can be significantly improved.

#### 8.3c Future Trends in Kelvin Wake Research

As our understanding of the Kelvin wake and its effects on ship motion continues to evolve, so too do the future trends in research in this area. These trends are driven by the need to improve ship design, propulsion systems, and operation to mitigate the effects of the Kelvin wake.

#### 8.3c.1 Advanced Ship Design and Configuration

Advanced ship design and configuration will continue to be a key area of research in the study of the Kelvin wake. As computational power continues to increase, so too will the ability to model and simulate the formation and effects of the Kelvin wake. This will allow for more detailed and accurate ship designs that minimize the formation of the Kelvin wake.

Moreover, advancements in materials science and engineering will also play a role. The development of new materials with improved hydrodynamic properties can help to reduce the formation of the Kelvin wake. For instance, the use of smart materials that can adapt to changing hydrodynamic conditions could be explored.

#### 8.3c.2 Advanced Propulsion Systems

Advanced propulsion systems will also be a key area of research in the study of the Kelvin wake. The development of new propulsion systems that can provide additional control and thrust, thereby reducing the effects of the Kelvin wake, will continue to be a focus.

Moreover, the integration of these advanced propulsion systems with ship design and configuration will also be a key area of research. This will involve the development of new control strategies that can optimize the operation of these advanced propulsion systems to minimize the effects of the Kelvin wake.

#### 8.3c.3 Advanced Ship Operation and Maintenance

Advanced ship operation and maintenance will also be a key area of research in the study of the Kelvin wake. The development of new maintenance strategies that can identify and address issues that contribute to the formation of the Kelvin wake will continue to be a focus.

Moreover, the development of new operation strategies that can optimize ship speed and maneuvering to minimize the effects of the Kelvin wake will also be a key area of research. This will involve the development of new control strategies that can optimize ship speed and maneuvering to minimize the effects of the Kelvin wake.

In conclusion, the future trends in Kelvin wake research are driven by the need to improve ship design, propulsion systems, and operation. As our understanding of the Kelvin wake continues to evolve, so too will these trends, driving further advancements in the field.

We have learned that the Kelvin wake is a phenomenon that is deeply rooted in the principles of fluid dynamics and wave propagation. It is a result of the interaction between the ship's hull and the surrounding water, and it can have profound effects on the ship's performance and the operation of offshore energy systems.

We have also seen how the Kelvin wake can be modeled and predicted using mathematical equations and computational models. These tools are invaluable for understanding and predicting the behavior of the Kelvin wake, and for designing and optimizing ships and offshore energy systems.

In conclusion, the study of the ship Kelvin wake is a rich and rewarding field that offers many opportunities for further research and application. It is a field that is constantly evolving, driven by advances in technology and our deepening understanding of fluid dynamics and wave propagation.

## Chapter: Chapter 9: Ship Wave Radiation

### Introduction

The study of wave radiation from ships is a critical aspect of ocean engineering. It is a complex field that involves the interaction of waves with the ship's hull, the surrounding water, and the atmosphere. This chapter, "Ship Wave Radiation," aims to provide a comprehensive guide to understanding and analyzing this phenomenon.

Wave radiation from ships is a significant factor in the design and operation of ships. It can affect the ship's stability, maneuverability, and overall performance. Understanding wave radiation is crucial for engineers and designers to optimize ship design and operation.

In this chapter, we will delve into the fundamental principles that govern wave radiation from ships. We will explore the mathematical models that describe wave radiation, including the Rayleigh theory and the Taylor theory. These theories provide a mathematical framework for understanding wave radiation, and they are essential tools for engineers and researchers in the field.

We will also discuss the practical implications of wave radiation. This includes its effects on ship stability and maneuverability, as well as its impact on the surrounding environment. We will also explore how wave radiation can be measured and analyzed in real-world scenarios.

This chapter will also touch on the latest research and developments in the field of wave radiation from ships. This includes advancements in computational models and experimental techniques, as well as new insights into the underlying physics of wave radiation.

#### 8.3b Methods to Mitigate Kelvin Wake Effects on Ship Motion

The effects of the Kelvin wake on ship motion can be significant and can pose challenges for ship design and operation. However, there are several methods that can be used to mitigate these effects.

#### 8.3b.1 Ship Design

One of the most effective ways to mitigate the effects of the Kelvin wake is through ship design. By incorporating features such as bulbous bows and skegs, the formation of the Kelvin wake can be reduced, thereby reducing the increase in drag and changes in hydrodynamic forces. These features can also help to reduce the noise and vibration levels on the ship.

#### 8.3b.2 Ship Operation

In addition to ship design, there are also methods that can be used during ship operation to mitigate the effects of the Kelvin wake. For example, by adjusting the ship's speed and course, the formation of the Kelvin wake can be minimized. This can be particularly effective in situations where the ship is operating in high-speed or high-wave conditions.

#### 8.3b.3 Ship Equipment

The effects of the Kelvin wake can also be mitigated through the use of specialized equipment. For example, the Extended Kalman filter, a mathematical model used for state estimation, can be used to predict and compensate for the effects of the Kelvin wake on ship motion. This can help to improve the ship's performance and stability, particularly in challenging conditions.

#### 8.3b.4 Ship Maintenance

Regular maintenance and inspection of the ship can also help to mitigate the effects of the Kelvin wake. By identifying and addressing any issues with the ship's hull or propulsion system, the formation of the Kelvin wake can be reduced, thereby reducing the increase in drag and changes in hydrodynamic forces.

In conclusion, while the Kelvin wake can pose significant challenges for ship design and operation, there are several methods that can be used to mitigate its effects. By incorporating these methods into ship design, operation, and maintenance, the effects of the Kelvin wake can be minimized, thereby improving the performance and safety of ships.

We have also discussed the practical implications of these phenomena for ship design and operation, and have highlighted the importance of understanding and predicting Kelvin wakes in order to optimize ship performance and safety.

The Kelvin wake is a critical aspect of ship hydrodynamics, and its study is essential for anyone involved in the design, operation, or analysis of ships. In conclusion, the study of ship Kelvin wakes is a rich and rewarding field, offering many opportunities for further research and application. Ships, as they move through the water, generate waves that propagate away from the vessel. For example, we will discuss how wave radiation can affect the stability and maneuverability of a ship, and how it can interact with other waves in the ocean to create complex wave patterns. #### 8.3c Case Studies of Kelvin Wake Effects on Ship Motion

In this section, we will explore some case studies that illustrate the effects of the Kelvin wake on ship motion. These case studies will provide a more concrete understanding of the concepts discussed in the previous sections.

#### 8.3c.1 Case Study 1: The E-Ship 1

The E-Ship 1, a hybrid electric-diesel ship, provides an excellent example of the effects of the Kelvin wake on ship motion. The ship, designed by Enercon, is equipped with a propulsion system that combines a diesel engine and an electric motor. This allows the ship to operate in both diesel and electric modes, providing flexibility in terms of speed and power consumption.

The performance results for the E-Ship 1, including sea-keeping and wind power, were published by Enercon on 23 September 2013. These results provide valuable insights into the effects of the Kelvin wake on the ship's motion. The data shows that the ship's motion was significantly affected by the Kelvin wake, particularly in terms of changes in hydrodynamic forces and noise and vibration levels.

#### 8.3c.2 Case Study 2: The Project 22160 Patrol Ship

The Project 22160 patrol ship, a Russian naval vessel, provides another example of the effects of the Kelvin wake on ship motion. The ship is equipped with a diesel engine and a propeller, similar to many other ships. However, the ship's design includes several features that aim to mitigate the effects of the Kelvin wake, such as a bulbous bow and skegs.

The ship's performance data, including its speed and maneuverability, can be used to assess the effectiveness of these features in mitigating the effects of the Kelvin wake. This data can also be used to compare the ship's performance with that of other ships, providing valuable insights into the role of the Kelvin wake in ship motion.

#### 8.3c.3 Case Study 3: The Extended Kalman Filter

The Extended Kalman Filter (EKF) provides a mathematical model that can be used to predict and compensate for the effects of the Kelvin wake on ship motion. The EKF is a powerful tool that can be used to estimate the state of a ship, including its position, velocity, and acceleration.

The EKF can be used to estimate the effects of the Kelvin wake on ship motion by incorporating a model of the Kelvin wake into the filter. This model can be based on empirical data, such as the data for the E-Ship 1 and the Project 22160 patrol ship, or on theoretical models, such as the equations for the Kelvin wake discussed in the previous sections.

By using the EKF to estimate the effects of the Kelvin wake, ship designers and operators can make more informed decisions about ship design and operation. This can help to mitigate the effects of the Kelvin wake on ship motion, improving the ship's performance and safety.

Understanding these factors and their interactions is crucial for predicting and mitigating the effects of the Kelvin wake on offshore energy systems.

We have also discussed the challenges and potential solutions for managing the Kelvin wake. These include the use of advanced ship design and control techniques, as well as the development of more robust and resilient offshore energy systems. While these solutions are not without their challenges, they offer promising avenues for reducing the impact of the Kelvin wake on offshore energy systems.

In conclusion, the study of the ship Kelvin wake is a vital aspect of ocean wave interaction with ships and offshore energy systems. It is a complex and dynamic field that requires a deep understanding of ocean dynamics, ship design, and offshore energy systems. With continued research and development, we can better understand and manage the Kelvin wake, leading to improved performance and reliability of offshore energy systems.

## Chapter: Chapter 9: Ship Wave Radiation

### Introduction

The interaction of waves with ships is a complex and fascinating field of study. It is a critical area of research for the design and operation of ships, as well as for the understanding of ocean dynamics. This chapter, "Ship Wave Radiation," delves into the intricate details of this interaction, focusing on the radiation of waves from ships.

Ship wave radiation is a phenomenon that occurs when a ship moves through the water, creating waves that propagate away from the ship. These waves can have significant impacts on the ship's performance, as well as on the surrounding marine environment. Understanding the mechanisms of ship wave radiation is crucial for predicting and mitigating these impacts.

In this chapter, we will explore the fundamental principles that govern ship wave radiation, including the physics of wave generation and propagation. We will also discuss the mathematical models used to describe these phenomena, such as the Taylor's hypothesis and the Taylor's series method. These models will be presented in the popular Markdown format, using the MathJax library for rendering mathematical expressions.

We will also delve into the practical implications of ship wave radiation, discussing its effects on ship design and operation. This includes the impact of wave radiation on ship stability, maneuverability, and energy efficiency. We will also explore how wave radiation can affect the performance of offshore energy systems, such as wind turbines and wave energy converters.

Finally, we will discuss the current state of research in ship wave radiation, highlighting the latest advancements and future directions in this field. This will include a discussion of the challenges and opportunities in this area, as well as the potential for future research collaborations.

This chapter aims to provide a comprehensive guide to ship wave radiation, suitable for both students and professionals in the field of ocean engineering. It is our hope that this guide will serve as a valuable resource for those seeking to understand and apply the principles of ship wave radiation in their work.




### Introduction

In this chapter, we will delve into the fascinating world of linear wave-body interaction. This topic is of great importance in the field of ocean engineering, as it deals with the interaction of waves with various structures and systems in the ocean. The understanding of this interaction is crucial for the design and operation of ships, offshore energy systems, and other marine structures.

Linear wave-body interaction is a complex phenomenon that involves the transfer of energy and momentum between waves and bodies. This interaction can be linear or nonlinear, depending on the nature of the waves and the bodies involved. In this chapter, we will focus on linear wave-body interaction, which is the simplest and most common type of interaction.

The study of linear wave-body interaction is based on the principles of linear wave theory, which is a mathematical model that describes the propagation of waves in the ocean. This theory is based on the assumptions that the waves are small, the water is deep, and the waves are not affected by the presence of the body. These assumptions allow us to derive simple equations that describe the interaction between waves and bodies.

We will begin this chapter by introducing the basic concepts of linear wave theory, including the wave equation and the wave-body interaction equation. We will then discuss the different types of bodies that can interact with waves, such as ships, offshore energy systems, and marine structures. We will also explore the different types of waves that can interact with these bodies, such as wind waves, swells, and tsunamis.

Next, we will delve into the various methods used to study linear wave-body interaction, such as analytical methods, numerical methods, and experimental methods. We will also discuss the advantages and limitations of each method, and how they can be combined to provide a more comprehensive understanding of the interaction.

Finally, we will discuss the practical applications of linear wave-body interaction, such as ship design, offshore energy systems, and marine structure design. We will also touch upon the challenges and future directions in this field, such as the effects of nonlinear waves and the need for more accurate and efficient methods of analysis.

In summary, this chapter aims to provide a comprehensive guide to linear wave-body interaction, covering the fundamental principles, methods, and applications of this important topic. Whether you are a student, a researcher, or a professional in the field of ocean engineering, we hope that this chapter will serve as a valuable resource for understanding and applying the principles of linear wave-body interaction.




### Subsection: 9.1a Definition of Linear Wave-Body Forces

Linear wave-body forces refer to the forces exerted by a wave on a body, which are directly proportional to the wave amplitude. These forces can be either hydrodynamic or aerodynamic, depending on whether the wave is in the water or in the air. 

#### Hydrodynamic Forces

Hydrodynamic forces are the forces exerted by a wave on a body immersed in a fluid, such as water. These forces can be further divided into two types: hydrodynamic drag and hydrodynamic lift. 

Hydrodynamic drag is the force that opposes the motion of the body in the direction of the wave propagation. It is caused by the friction between the body and the fluid, and it is proportional to the square of the wave amplitude. Mathematically, it can be expressed as:

$$
F_D = \frac{1}{2} C_D \rho g A^2
$$

where $F_D$ is the hydrodynamic drag force, $C_D$ is the drag coefficient, $\rho$ is the fluid density, $g$ is the acceleration due to gravity, and $A$ is the wave amplitude.

Hydrodynamic lift is the force that acts perpendicular to the direction of the wave propagation. It is caused by the pressure difference between the front and the back of the body, and it is proportional to the cube of the wave amplitude. Mathematically, it can be expressed as:

$$
F_L = \frac{1}{2} C_L \rho g A^3
$$

where $F_L$ is the hydrodynamic lift force, $C_L$ is the lift coefficient, and the other variables have the same meaning as in the equation for hydrodynamic drag.

#### Aerodynamic Forces

Aerodynamic forces are the forces exerted by a wave on a body immersed in a gas, such as air. These forces can also be divided into two types: aerodynamic drag and aerodynamic lift. 

Aerodynamic drag is the force that opposes the motion of the body in the direction of the wave propagation. It is caused by the friction between the body and the gas, and it is proportional to the square of the wave amplitude. Mathematically, it can be expressed as:

$$
F_D = \frac{1}{2} C_D \rho A^2
$$

where $F_D$ is the aerodynamic drag force, $C_D$ is the drag coefficient, $\rho$ is the gas density, and $A$ is the wave amplitude.

Aerodynamic lift is the force that acts perpendicular to the direction of the wave propagation. It is caused by the pressure difference between the front and the back of the body, and it is proportional to the cube of the wave amplitude. Mathematically, it can be expressed as:

$$
F_L = \frac{1}{2} C_L \rho A^3
$$

where $F_L$ is the aerodynamic lift force, $C_L$ is the lift coefficient, and the other variables have the same meaning as in the equation for aerodynamic drag.

In the next section, we will discuss the methods used to calculate these forces.




### Subsection: 9.1b Calculation of Linear Wave-Body Forces

The calculation of linear wave-body forces involves the application of the principles of fluid dynamics and aerodynamics. The forces are calculated based on the wave amplitude, the properties of the fluid or gas, and the geometry of the body. 

#### Hydrodynamic Forces

The calculation of hydrodynamic forces involves the application of the principles of fluid dynamics. The hydrodynamic drag force, $F_D$, and lift force, $F_L$, can be calculated using the equations provided in the previous section. These equations involve the wave amplitude, the drag and lift coefficients, the fluid density, and the acceleration due to gravity. 

The drag coefficient, $C_D$, and lift coefficient, $C_L$, are dimensionless quantities that depend on the shape of the body and the properties of the fluid. They can be determined experimentally or theoretically. 

#### Aerodynamic Forces

The calculation of aerodynamic forces involves the application of the principles of aerodynamics. The aerodynamic drag force, $F_D$, and lift force, $F_L$, can be calculated using similar equations to those for hydrodynamic forces. However, the properties of the gas (air) are used instead of the fluid properties. 

The aerodynamic drag coefficient, $C_D$, and lift coefficient, $C_L$, are also dimensionless quantities that depend on the shape of the body and the properties of the gas. They can be determined experimentally or theoretically. 

In the next section, we will discuss the methods for determining the drag and lift coefficients for both hydrodynamic and aerodynamic forces.




#### 9.1c Effects of Linear Wave-Body Forces on Ship Dynamics

The effects of linear wave-body forces on ship dynamics are significant and complex. These forces can cause a ship to heave, pitch, and roll, which can affect the ship's stability and maneuverability. The magnitude and direction of these forces depend on the wave amplitude, the properties of the fluid or gas, and the geometry of the ship.

#### Heave

Heave is the vertical motion of a ship caused by wave-body forces. This motion can be calculated using the equations for hydrodynamic and aerodynamic forces. The heave force, $F_H$, can be calculated using the equation:

$$
F_H = \frac{1}{2} \rho g A \sin(\omega t - k x)
$$

where $\rho$ is the fluid density, $g$ is the acceleration due to gravity, $A$ is the wave amplitude, $\omega$ is the angular frequency, $k$ is the wave number, and $x$ is the horizontal position of the ship.

The heave force can cause a ship to rise and fall, which can affect the ship's stability. This is particularly important for ships operating in rough seas or high winds.

#### Pitch

Pitch is the rotational motion of a ship about its longitudinal axis caused by wave-body forces. This motion can be calculated using the equations for hydrodynamic and aerodynamic forces. The pitch moment, $M_P$, can be calculated using the equation:

$$
M_P = \frac{1}{2} \rho g A \sin(\omega t - k x) \cdot L
$$

where $L$ is the length of the ship.

The pitch moment can cause a ship to roll, which can affect the ship's stability and maneuverability. This is particularly important for ships operating in waves or wind.

#### Roll

Roll is the rotational motion of a ship about its transverse axis caused by wave-body forces. This motion can be calculated using the equations for hydrodynamic and aerodynamic forces. The roll moment, $M_R$, can be calculated using the equation:

$$
M_R = \frac{1}{2} \rho g A \sin(\omega t - k x) \cdot B
$$

where $B$ is the breadth of the ship.

The roll moment can cause a ship to roll, which can affect the ship's stability and maneuverability. This is particularly important for ships operating in waves or wind.

In the next section, we will discuss the methods for determining the wave-body forces and their effects on ship dynamics.




#### 9.2a Definition of Added Mass and Damping Coefficients

In the study of wave-body interaction, two key parameters are the added mass and damping coefficients. These parameters are crucial in understanding the behavior of a body in a fluid medium, particularly in the context of ship dynamics and offshore energy systems.

#### Added Mass

The added mass, $m_a$, is a concept in fluid dynamics that describes the increase in mass of a body when it is immersed in a fluid. This increase in mass is due to the fluid displacement caused by the body's motion. The added mass can be calculated using the equation:

$$
m_a = \rho_f \cdot V_f
$$

where $\rho_f$ is the fluid density and $V_f$ is the volume of the fluid displaced by the body.

The added mass can significantly affect the dynamics of a body in a fluid medium. For instance, in the case of a ship, the added mass can increase the ship's mass and inertia, which can affect the ship's response to wave forces.

#### Damping Coefficients

Damping coefficients, often denoted as $C$ and $D$, are parameters that describe the rate at which a body loses energy in a fluid medium. These coefficients are crucial in understanding the behavior of a body in a wave field.

The damping coefficients can be calculated using the equations:

$$
C = \frac{1}{2} \rho_f \cdot V_f \cdot U_f
$$

$$
D = \frac{1}{2} \rho_f \cdot V_f \cdot V_f
$$

where $U_f$ is the velocity of the fluid and $V_f$ is the velocity of the body relative to the fluid.

The damping coefficients play a significant role in the dynamics of a body in a wave field. For instance, in the case of a ship, the damping coefficients can affect the ship's response to wave forces and the ship's natural frequency.

In the following sections, we will delve deeper into the calculation and application of these parameters in the context of wave-body interaction.

#### 9.2b Calculation of Added Mass and Damping Coefficients

The calculation of added mass and damping coefficients is a crucial step in understanding the behavior of a body in a fluid medium. These calculations are based on the principles of fluid dynamics and are essential in the design and analysis of ships and offshore energy systems.

##### Added Mass

The calculation of added mass involves determining the volume of the fluid displaced by the body and the density of the fluid. The volume of the fluid displaced by the body can be calculated using the equation:

$$
V_f = \int_{V_b} \rho_f dV
$$

where $V_b$ is the volume of the body and $\rho_f$ is the density of the fluid. The added mass can then be calculated using the equation:

$$
m_a = \rho_f \cdot V_f
$$

##### Damping Coefficients

The calculation of damping coefficients involves determining the velocity of the fluid and the velocity of the body relative to the fluid. The velocity of the fluid can be calculated using the equation:

$$
U_f = \frac{1}{2} \left( \frac{\partial \phi}{\partial x} + \frac{\partial \psi}{\partial y} \right)
$$

where $\phi$ and $\psi$ are the stream functions for the fluid velocity in the $x$ and $y$ directions, respectively. The velocity of the body relative to the fluid can be calculated using the equation:

$$
V_f = \frac{1}{2} \left( \frac{\partial \phi_b}{\partial x} + \frac{\partial \psi_b}{\partial y} \right)
$$

where $\phi_b$ and $\psi_b$ are the stream functions for the body velocity in the $x$ and $y$ directions, respectively. The damping coefficients can then be calculated using the equations:

$$
C = \frac{1}{2} \rho_f \cdot V_f \cdot U_f
$$

$$
D = \frac{1}{2} \rho_f \cdot V_f \cdot V_f
$$

It is important to note that the calculation of added mass and damping coefficients is a complex process that requires a deep understanding of fluid dynamics and the principles of wave-body interaction. These calculations are essential in the design and analysis of ships and offshore energy systems, and they play a crucial role in ensuring the safety and efficiency of these systems.

#### 9.2c Applications of Added Mass and Damping Coefficients

The added mass and damping coefficients play a significant role in the design and analysis of ships and offshore energy systems. These parameters are crucial in understanding the behavior of a body in a fluid medium and are essential in predicting the response of a system to wave forces.

##### Ship Design

In ship design, the added mass and damping coefficients are used to predict the response of the ship to wave forces. The added mass of the ship can affect its stability and maneuverability, while the damping coefficients can influence the ship's natural frequency and its response to wave forces. By accurately calculating these parameters, engineers can design ships that are more stable and maneuverable, and that can withstand higher wave forces.

##### Offshore Energy Systems

In the design of offshore energy systems, such as wind turbines and wave energy converters, the added mass and damping coefficients are used to predict the response of the system to wave forces. These parameters can affect the performance and reliability of the system, and can influence its ability to withstand wave forces. By accurately calculating these parameters, engineers can design systems that are more efficient and reliable, and that can operate in a wider range of wave conditions.

##### Wave-Body Interaction

The added mass and damping coefficients are also used in the study of wave-body interaction. This field involves the study of the interaction between waves and bodies in a fluid medium, and is crucial in understanding the behavior of ships and offshore energy systems in wave fields. By accurately calculating these parameters, researchers can gain a deeper understanding of wave-body interaction, and can develop more accurate models for predicting the behavior of ships and offshore energy systems in wave fields.

In conclusion, the added mass and damping coefficients are crucial parameters in the design and analysis of ships and offshore energy systems. These parameters are essential in predicting the response of a system to wave forces, and play a significant role in the study of wave-body interaction. By accurately calculating these parameters, engineers and researchers can design more efficient and reliable systems, and can gain a deeper understanding of wave-body interaction.
